If `get` is\n// successful, `Ready()` returns ready and `configuration()` returns the\n// `mergedConfiguration`; if `get` has failed more than `failureThreshold ` times,\n// `Ready()` returns not ready and `configuration()` returns nil configuration.\n// In an HA setup, the poller is consistent only if the `get` is\n// doing consistent read.\ntype poller struct {\n\t// a function to consistently read the latest configuration\n\tget getFunc\n\t// consistent read interval\n\t// read-only\n\tinterval time.Duration\n\t// if the number of consecutive read failure equals or exceeds the failureThreshold , the\n\t// configuration is regarded as not ready.\n\t// read-only\n\tfailureThreshold int\n\t// number of consecutive failures so far.\n\tfailures int\n\t// If the poller has passed the bootstrap phase. The poller is considered\n\t// bootstrapped either bootstrapGracePeriod after the first call of\n\t// configuration(), or when setConfigurationAndReady() is called, whichever\n\t// comes first.\n\tbootstrapped bool\n\t// configuration() retries bootstrapRetries times if poller is not bootstrapped\n\t// read-only\n\tbootstrapRetries int\n\t// Grace period for bootstrapping\n\t// read-only\n\tbootstrapGracePeriod time.Duration\n\tonce                 sync.Once\n\t// if the configuration is regarded as ready.\n\tready               bool\n\tmergedConfiguration runtime.Object\n\tlastErr             error\n\t// lock must be hold when reading/writing the data fields of poller.\n\tlock sync.RWMutex\n}\n\nfunc newPoller(get getFunc) *poller {\n\tp := poller{\n\t\tget:                  get,\n\t\tinterval:             defaultInterval,\n\t\tfailureThreshold:     defaultFailureThreshold,\n\t\tbootstrapRetries:     defaultBootstrapRetries,\n\t\tbootstrapGracePeriod: defaultBootstrapGraceperiod,\n\t}\n\treturn &p\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) lastError(err error) {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.lastErr = err\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) notReady() {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.ready = false\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) bootstrapping() {\n\t// bootstrapGracePeriod is read-only, so no lock is required\n\ttimer := time.NewTimer(a.bootstrapGracePeriod)\n\tgo func() {\n\t\tdefer timer.Stop()\n\t\t<-timer.C\n\t\ta.lock.Lock()\n\t\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\t\ta.bootstrapped = true\n\t}()\n}\n\n// If the poller is not bootstrapped yet, the configuration() gets a few chances\n// to retry. This hides transient failures during system startup.\nfunc (a *poller) configuration() (runtime.Object, error) {\n\ta.once.Do(a.bootstrapping)\n\ta.lock.RLock()\n\tdefer a.lock.RUnlock()\n\tretries := 1\n\tif !a.bootstrapped {\n\t\tretries = a.bootstrapRetries\n\t}\n\tfor count := 0; count < retries; count++ {\n\t\tif count > 0 {\n\t\t\ta.lock.RUnlock()\n\t\t\ttime.Sleep(a.interval)\n\t\t\ta.lock.RLock()\n\t\t}\n\t\tif a.ready {\n\t\t\treturn a.mergedConfiguration, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif a.lastErr != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, a.lastErr\n\t}\n\treturn nil, ErrNotReady\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) setConfigurationAndReady(value runtime.Object) {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.bootstrapped = true\n\ta.mergedConfiguration = value\n\ta.ready = true\n\ta.lastErr = nil\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n\tgo wait.Until(a.sync, a.interval, stopCh)\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) sync() {\n\tconfiguration, err := a.get()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\ta.failures++\n\t\ta.lastError(err)\n\t\tif a.failures >= a.failureThreshold {\n\t\t\ta.notReady()\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\ta.failures = 0\n\ta.setConfigurationAndReady(configuration)\n}\n","numLines":167,"startLine":1,"totalLines":167}}}

pipeline is implemented across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository, primarily in the staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver package. The architecture consists of three main layers: core admission interfaces, plugin implementations with webhook support, and request handler integration.\\n\\n## Core Admission Framework (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/)\\n\\nThe foundation is defined in interfaces.go, which declares three key interfaces:\\n- Interface: Base interface with a Handles(operation) method\\n- MutationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for mutating admission\\n- ValidationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Validate(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for validating admission\\n\\nThe chain.go file implements the actual admission chain execution through the chainAdmissionHandler type. It iterates through registered admission handlers, calling their Admit() methods for all MutationInterface implementations (lines 31-44), then Validate() methods for all ValidationInterface implementations (lines 47-60). The Handles() method (lines 63-70) enables filtering of operations.\\n\\nThe plugins.go file orchestrates chain construction via NewFromPlugins() (lines 127-163), which:\\n1. Iterates through enabled plugin names\\n2. Calls InitPlugin() to initialize each plugin with configuration\\n3. Wraps plugins with decorators (e.g., audit logging)\\n4. Constructs the chain handler from initialized plugins\\n5. Returns a wrapped chain via newReinvocationHandler() to support webhook re-invocation\\n\\nThe handler.go file provides the base Handler struct that manages supported operations via sets and a ReadyFunc for checking plugin readiness.\\n\\n## Chain Wrapping and Decoration\\n\\nThe reinvocation.go file wraps the chain handler to support webhook re-invocation policy. The reinvoker type (lines 27-29) calls Admit() twice if the reinvocation context indicates mutations occurred, allowing webhooks registered for re-invocation to be called again (lines 35-51).\\n\\nThe audit.go file adds audit logging via the WithAudit() decorator (line 39), which wraps the chain handler and logs admission annotations to audit events after Admit() and Validate() calls (lines 46-74).\\n\\nThe decorator.go file defines the Decorator interface for composing wrappers around admission handlers (lines 19-21), enabling inside-out application of decorators (line 32).\\n\\n## Webhook Implementation (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/)\\n\\nTwo webhook admission controller implementations exist:\\n\\n### Mutating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/mutating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing MutationInterface, registers as \\\"MutatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-76)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch() (lines 105-240) which:\\n  1. Retrieves mutating webhook configurations via webhook accessors\\n  2. Determines invocation eligibility based on resource selectors\\n  3. Calls each webhook via REST client\\n  4. Applies JSON patches to the object\\n  5. Tracks mutations for re-invocation\\n  6. Handles failure policies (Ignore vs Fail)\\n\\n### Validating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/validating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing ValidationInterface, registers as \\\"ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-68)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements validatingDispatcher.Dispatch() which:\\n  1. Retrieves validating webhook configurations\\n  2. Validates objects without mutations\\n  3. Supports parallel webhook invocation (unlike mutating)\\n  4. Handles rejections and audit annotations\\n\\nBoth use the generic webhook.go base implementation and interfaces.go Dispatcher interface.\\n\\n## Webhook Configuration Management (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/)\\n\\n- mutating_webhook_manager.go: NewMutatingWebhookConfigurationManager() creates a manager that lists MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects via informers (lines 53-89) and provides sorted webhook accessors with caching (lines 104-151)\\n- validating_webhook_manager.go: Analogous manager for ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects\\n- configuration_manager.go: Base polling mechanism for configuration synchronization\\n\\n## Kubernetes-Specific Initialization\\n\\n- pkg/kubeapiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for Kubernetes-specific plugins (WantsCloudConfig interface)\\n- pkg/controlplane/apiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for generic controlplane plugins (WantsQuotaConfiguration, WantsExcludedAdmissionResources interfaces)\\n\\n## Execution Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: NewFromPlugins() constructs the admission chain from enabled plugins, wraps with reinvocationHandler, wrapped with audit logging\\n2. **Request Processing**: API request handlers invoke the chain\\n3. **Mutating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() iterates handlers, calling Admit() on MutationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Admit() delegates to mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n4. **Validating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() iterates handlers, calling Validate() on ValidationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Validate() delegates to validatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n5. **Re-invocation**: If mutations occurred and re-invocation policy is set, the reinvoker calls Admit() again\\n6. **Audit Logging**: auditHandler.Admit/Validate() logs admission annotations to audit events\\n\\nThis architecture allows for:\\n- Extensible admission control via registered plugins\\n- Dynamic webhook configuration without API server restart\\n- Ordered, deterministic execution of admission phases\\n- Fine-grained failure policies per webhook\\n- Re-invocation of webhooks when mutations occur\\n- Audit trail of admission decisions\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1385,"cache_read_input_tokens":61869,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1385},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b58197cc-5f84-4b98-ac73-70f8d5314154","uuid":"3485d50b-02aa-415f-9678-0fb17aff33af"}

The architecture consists of three main layers: core admission interfaces, plugin implementations with webhook support, and request handler integration.\\n\\n## Core Admission Framework (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/)\\n\\nThe foundation is defined in interfaces.go, which declares three key interfaces:\\n- Interface: Base interface with a Handles(operation) method\\n- MutationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for mutating admission\\n- ValidationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Validate(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for validating admission\\n\\nThe chain.go file implements the actual admission chain execution through the chainAdmissionHandler type. It iterates through registered admission handlers, calling their Admit() methods for all MutationInterface implementations (lines 31-44), then Validate() methods for all ValidationInterface implementations (lines 47-60). The Handles() method (lines 63-70) enables filtering of operations.\\n\\nThe plugins.go file orchestrates chain construction via NewFromPlugins() (lines 127-163), which:\\n1. Iterates through enabled plugin names\\n2. Calls InitPlugin() to initialize each plugin with configuration\\n3. Wraps plugins with decorators (e.g., audit logging)\\n4. Constructs the chain handler from initialized plugins\\n5. Returns a wrapped chain via newReinvocationHandler() to support webhook re-invocation\\n\\nThe handler.go file provides the base Handler struct that manages supported operations via sets and a ReadyFunc for checking plugin readiness.\\n\\n## Chain Wrapping and Decoration\\n\\nThe reinvocation.go file wraps the chain handler to support webhook re-invocation policy. The reinvoker type (lines 27-29) calls Admit() twice if the reinvocation context indicates mutations occurred, allowing webhooks registered for re-invocation to be called again (lines 35-51).\\n\\nThe audit.go file adds audit logging via the WithAudit() decorator (line 39), which wraps the chain handler and logs admission annotations to audit events after Admit() and Validate() calls (lines 46-74).\\n\\nThe decorator.go file defines the Decorator interface for composing wrappers around admission handlers (lines 19-21), enabling inside-out application of decorators (line 32).\\n\\n## Webhook Implementation (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/)\\n\\nTwo webhook admission controller implementations exist:\\n\\n### Mutating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/mutating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing MutationInterface, registers as \\\"MutatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-76)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch() (lines 105-240) which:\\n  1. Retrieves mutating webhook configurations via webhook accessors\\n  2. Determines invocation eligibility based on resource selectors\\n  3. Calls each webhook via REST client\\n  4. Applies JSON patches to the object\\n  5. Tracks mutations for re-invocation\\n  6. Handles failure policies (Ignore vs Fail)\\n\\n### Validating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/validating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing ValidationInterface, registers as \\\"ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-68)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements validatingDispatcher.Dispatch() which:\\n  1. Retrieves validating webhook configurations\\n  2. Validates objects without mutations\\n  3. Supports parallel webhook invocation (unlike mutating)\\n  4. Handles rejections and audit annotations\\n\\nBoth use the generic webhook.go base implementation and interfaces.go Dispatcher interface.\\n\\n## Webhook Configuration Management (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/)\\n\\n- mutating_webhook_manager.go: NewMutatingWebhookConfigurationManager() creates a manager that lists MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects via informers (lines 53-89) and provides sorted webhook accessors with caching (lines 104-151)\\n- validating_webhook_manager.go: Analogous manager for ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects\\n- configuration_manager.go: Base polling mechanism for configuration synchronization\\n\\n## Kubernetes-Specific Initialization\\n\\n- pkg/kubeapiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for Kubernetes-specific plugins (WantsCloudConfig interface)\\n- pkg/controlplane/apiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for generic controlplane plugins (WantsQuotaConfiguration, WantsExcludedAdmissionResources interfaces)\\n\\n## Execution Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: NewFromPlugins() constructs the admission chain from enabled plugins, wraps with reinvocationHandler, wrapped with audit logging\\n2. **Request Processing**: API request handlers invoke the chain\\n3. **Mutating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() iterates handlers, calling Admit() on MutationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Admit() delegates to mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n4. **Validating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() iterates handlers, calling Validate() on ValidationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Validate() delegates to validatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n5. **Re-invocation**: If mutations occurred and re-invocation policy is set, the reinvoker calls Admit() again\\n6. **Audit Logging**: auditHandler.Admit/Validate() logs admission annotations to audit events\\n\\nThis architecture allows for:\\n- Extensible admission control via registered plugins\\n- Dynamic webhook configuration without API server restart\\n- Ordered, deterministic execution of admission phases\\n- Fine-grained failure policies per webhook\\n- Re-invocation of webhooks when mutations occur\\n- Audit trail of admission decisions\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
